<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">University of British Columbia</h1> <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div> <div id="contentSub"></div>

<p>The <b>University of British Columbia</b> (<b>UBC</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a> <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university">research university</a> with campuses in <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kelowna" title="Kelowna">Kelowna</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a>. Established in 1908, UBC is British Columbia's oldest university. The university is ranked among the top 20 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_universities" title="Public universities">public universities</a> worldwide and top three<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> in Canada.  With an annual research budget of $600 million (one of the largest in Canada), UBC funds over 8,000 projects a year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UBCfacts_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-UBCfacts-4">[4]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Vancouver campus is situated about 10 km (6 mi) west of <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Vancouver" title="Downtown Vancouver">Downtown Vancouver</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-facts1_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-facts1-9">[9]</a></sup> UBC is home to <a href="/wiki/TRIUMF" title="TRIUMF">TRIUMF</a>, Canada's national laboratory for <a href="/wiki/Particle_physics" title="Particle physics">particle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_physics" title="Nuclear physics">nuclear physics</a>, which houses the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Cyclotron" title="Cyclotron">cyclotron</a>. In addition to the <a href="/wiki/Peter_Wall_Institute_for_Advanced_Studies" title="Peter Wall Institute for Advanced Studies">Peter Wall Institute for Advanced Studies</a> and Stuart Blusson Quantum Matter Institute, UBC and the <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Society" title="Max Planck Society">Max Planck Society</a> collectively established the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Institute" title="Max Planck Institute">Max Planck Institute</a> in North America, specializing in <a href="/wiki/Quantum_materials" title="Quantum materials">quantum materials</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> One of the largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Research_libraries" title="Research libraries">research libraries</a> in Canada, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UBC_Library" title="UBC Library">UBC Library</a> system has over 9.9 million volumes among its 21 branches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_British_Columbia_Okanagan" title="University of British Columbia Okanagan">Okanagan campus</a>, acquired in 2005, is located in Kelowna, British Columbia.
</p><p>UBC is internationally recognized in STEM fields, ranking 10th in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Computer_Science" title="Computer Science">Computer Science</a>, 5th in <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">Ecology</a>, 22nd in <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">Mathematics</a>, and 25th in <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">Medicine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> In the humanities, the university ranks 22nd in <a href="/wiki/Literature" title="Literature">Literature</a>, 28th in <a href="/wiki/Law" title="Law">Law</a>, and 23rd in <a href="/wiki/Economics" title="Economics">Economics</a> worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup>
</p><p>As of  2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, eight <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_by_university_affiliation" title="List of Nobel laureates by university affiliation">Nobel</a> laureates, 71 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholarships" title="Rhodes Scholarships">Rhodes</a> scholars, 65 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olympic_medals" title="Olympic medals">Olympians</a>, eight Fellows in both <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Arts_%26_Sciences" title="American Academy of Arts &amp; Sciences">American Academy of Arts &amp; Sciences</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society" title="Royal Society">Royal Society</a>, and 208 Fellows to the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society_of_Canada" title="Royal Society of Canada">Royal Society of Canada</a> have been affiliated with UBC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UBCfacts_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-UBCfacts-4">[4]</a></sup> Three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_prime_ministers" title="Canadian prime ministers">Canadian prime ministers</a>, including Canada's first female prime minister <a href="/wiki/Kim_Campbell" title="Kim Campbell">Kim Campbell</a> and current prime minister <a href="/wiki/Justin_Trudeau" title="Justin Trudeau">Justin Trudeau</a> have been educated at UBC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foundation_and_early_years">Foundation and early years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Foundation and early years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="rquote pullquote floatright" role="presentation" style="border-collapse:collapse; border-style:none; float:right; margin:0.5em 0.75em; width:33%;">
<tbody><tr style="text-align:left; vertical-align:top;">
<td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; width:0.5em; line-height: 1em;">“
</td>
<td style="padding:0 10px;">The University shall... provide for: Such instruction in all branches of liberal education as may enable students to become proficient in... science, commerce, arts, literature, law, medicine, and all other branches of knowledge
</td>
<td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; text-align:right; vertical-align:bottom; width:0.5em; line-height: 1em;">”
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td class="rquotecite" colspan="3" style="padding-top:10px; font-size:smaller; line-height:normal; text-align:right;"><cite>— An Act to Establish and Incorporate a University for the Province of British Columbia, <i>Acts of 1908, Chapter 53</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></cite>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UBC_Fairview_campus_(c._1917).gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="426" data-file-width="742" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/UBC_Fairview_campus_%28c._1917%29.gif/220px-UBC_Fairview_campus_%28c._1917%29.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/UBC_Fairview_campus_%28c._1917%29.gif/330px-UBC_Fairview_campus_%28c._1917%29.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/UBC_Fairview_campus_%28c._1917%29.gif/440px-UBC_Fairview_campus_%28c._1917%29.gif 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UBC_Fairview_campus_(c._1917).gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of the UBC Fairview campus from the roof of King Edward High School (c. 1917) (Vancouver, British Columbia) (photo by Canadian Photo Co.)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sharp_and_Thompson_proposed_plan_for_the_UBC_Point_Grey_campus.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="843" data-file-width="1491" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Sharp_and_Thompson_proposed_plan_for_the_UBC_Point_Grey_campus.jpg/220px-Sharp_and_Thompson_proposed_plan_for_the_UBC_Point_Grey_campus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Sharp_and_Thompson_proposed_plan_for_the_UBC_Point_Grey_campus.jpg/330px-Sharp_and_Thompson_proposed_plan_for_the_UBC_Point_Grey_campus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Sharp_and_Thompson_proposed_plan_for_the_UBC_Point_Grey_campus.jpg/440px-Sharp_and_Thompson_proposed_plan_for_the_UBC_Point_Grey_campus.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sharp_and_Thompson_proposed_plan_for_the_UBC_Point_Grey_campus.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Original 1914 plan of the UBC campus, by architects Sharp and Thompson</div></div></div>
<p>In 1877, six years after British Columbia joined Canada, the Superintendent of Education, John Jessop, submitted a proposal for the formation of a provincial university. The provincial legislature passed <i>An Act Respecting the University of British Columbia</i> in 1890, but disagreements arose over whether to build the university on <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Island" title="Vancouver Island">Vancouver Island</a> or the mainland.
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Columbia_University_Act" title="British Columbia University Act">British Columbia University Act</a> of 1908 formally called a provincial university into being, although its location was not specified.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-21">[21]</a></sup>  The governance was modelled on the provincial University of Toronto Act of 1906 which created a bicameral system of university government consisting of a senate (faculty), responsible for academic policy, and a board of governors (citizens) exercising exclusive control over financial policy and having formal authority in all other matters. The president, appointed by the board, was to provide a link between the two bodies and to perform institutional leadership.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-21">[21]</a></sup> The Act constituted a twenty-one member senate with Francis Carter-Cotton of Vancouver as Chancellor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup>
</p><p>Before the University Act, there had been several attempts at creating a degree-granting university with help from the Universities of <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto" title="University of Toronto">Toronto</a> and <a href="/wiki/McGill_University" title="McGill University">McGill</a>. Columbian College in New Westminster, through its affiliation with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Victoria_University_in_the_University_of_Toronto" title="Victoria University in the University of Toronto">Victoria College of the University of Toronto</a>, began to offer university-level credit at the turn-of-the-century, but McGill came to dominate higher education in the early 1900s.
</p><p>
Building on a successful affiliation between Vancouver and Victoria high schools with McGill University, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Marshall_Tory" title="Henry Marshall Tory">Henry Marshall Tory</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tory_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tory-23">[23]</a></sup> helped establish the McGill University College of British Columbia. From 1906 to 1915, McGill BC (as it was called) operated as a private institution providing the first few years toward a degree at McGill University or elsewhere. The Henry Marshall Tory Medal was established in 1941 by Tory, founding President of the University of Alberta and of the National Research Council of Canada, and a co-founder of Carleton University. </p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Carleton_pres_Tory.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="476" data-file-width="360" height="291" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Carleton_pres_Tory.jpg/220px-Carleton_pres_Tory.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Carleton_pres_Tory.jpg/330px-Carleton_pres_Tory.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b5/Carleton_pres_Tory.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Carleton_pres_Tory.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Henry_Marshall_Tory" title="Henry Marshall Tory">Henry Marshall Tory</a></div></div></div>
<p>In the meantime, appeals were made to the government to revive the earlier legislation for a provincial institution, leading to the University Endowment Act in 1907, and the University Act in 1908. In 1910 the Point Grey site was chosen, and the government appointed Dr. <a href="/wiki/Frank_Wesbrook" title="Frank Wesbrook">Frank Fairchild Wesbrook</a> as President in 1913, and <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Klinck" title="Leonard Klinck">Leonard Klinck</a> as Dean of Agriculture in 1914. A declining economy and the outbreak of war in August 1914 compelled the University to postpone plans for building at Point Grey, and instead the former McGill University College site at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fairview_(Vancouver)" title="Fairview (Vancouver)">Fairview</a> became home to the University until 1925. On the first day of lectures was September 30, 1915, the new independent university absorbed McGill University College. The University of British Columbia awarded its first degrees in 1916,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-21">[21]</a></sup> and Klinck became the second President in 1919, serving until 1940.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Move_to_Point_Grey">Move to Point Grey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Move to Point Grey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>World War I dominated campus life, and the student body was "decimated" by enlistments for active service, with three hundred UBC students in Company "D" alone. By the war's end, 697 members of the University had enlisted. 109 students graduated in the three war-time congregations, all but one in the Faculty of Arts and Science.
</p><p>By 1920, the university had only three faculties: Arts, Applied Science, and Agriculture (with Departments of <a href="/wiki/Agronomy" title="Agronomy">Agronomy</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Animal_Husbandry" title="Animal Husbandry">Animal Husbandry</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dairying" title="Dairying">Dairying</a>, Horticulture and Poultry). It only awarded the degrees of Bachelor of Arts (BA), <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Applied_Science" title="Bachelor of Applied Science">Bachelor of Applied Science</a> (BASc), and Bachelor of Science in Agriculture (BSA).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> There were 576 male students and 386 female students in the 1920–21 winter session, but only 64 academic staff, including 6 women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the early part of the 20th century, professional education expanded beyond the traditional fields of theology, law and medicine. Although UBC did not offer degrees in these fields, it began to offer degrees in new professional areas such as engineering, agriculture, nursing and school teaching. It also introduced graduate training based on the German-inspired American model of specialized course work and the completion of a research thesis, with students completing M.A. degrees in natural sciences, social sciences and humanities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_21-3"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-21">[21]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UBC_Great_Trek_at_Granville_and_Georgia_streets.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="538" data-file-width="703" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/UBC_Great_Trek_at_Granville_and_Georgia_streets.gif/220px-UBC_Great_Trek_at_Granville_and_Georgia_streets.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/UBC_Great_Trek_at_Granville_and_Georgia_streets.gif/330px-UBC_Great_Trek_at_Granville_and_Georgia_streets.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/UBC_Great_Trek_at_Granville_and_Georgia_streets.gif/440px-UBC_Great_Trek_at_Granville_and_Georgia_streets.gif 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UBC_Great_Trek_at_Granville_and_Georgia_streets.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Students march down Granville street during the Great Trek</div></div></div>
<p>In 1922, the twelve-hundred-strong student body embarked on a "Build the University" campaign. Students marched through the streets of Vancouver to draw attention to their plight, enlist popular support, and embarrass the government. Fifty-six thousand signatures were presented at legislature in support of the campaign, which was ultimately successful. On September 22, 1925, lectures began at the new Point Grey campus. Except for the Library, Science and Power House buildings, all the campus buildings were temporary constructions. Students built two playing fields, but the University had no dormitories and no social centre. Still, the University continued to grow steadily.
</p><p>Soon, however, the effects of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression_in_Canada" title="Great Depression in Canada">depression</a> began to be felt. The provincial government, upon which the University depended heavily, cut the annual grant severely. In 1932–33, salaries were cut by up to 23%. Posts remained vacant, and a few faculty lost their jobs. Most graduate courses were dropped. In 1935, the University established the Department of Extension. Just as things began to improve, World War II began and Canada declared war on September 10, 1939. Soon afterwards, University President Klinck wrote:
</p>
<blockquote><p>From the day of the declaration of war, the University has been prepared to put at the disposal of the Government all possible assistance by way of laboratories, equipment and trained personnel, insofar as such action is consistent with the maintenance of reasonably efficient instructional standards. To do less would be unthinkable.</p></blockquote>
<p>Heavy rains and melting snowfall eroded a deep ravine across the north end of the campus, in the Grand Campus Washout of 1935. The campus did not have <a href="/wiki/Storm_drain" title="Storm drain">storm drains</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Surface_runoff" title="Surface runoff">surface runoff</a> went down a ravine to the beach. When the University carved a ditch to drain flooding on University Avenue, the rush of water steepened the ravine and eroded it back as fast as 10 feet (3.0 m) per hour. The resulting gully eventually consumed 100,000 cubic yards (76,455 m<sup>3</sup>), two bridges, and buildings near <a href="/wiki/Green_College,_University_of_British_Columbia" title="Green College, University of British Columbia">Graham House</a>. The university was closed for 4 and a half days. Afterwards, the gully was filled with debris from a nearby landslide, and only traces are visible today.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams_1966_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Williams_1966-26">[26]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Recruit_training" title="Recruit training">Military training</a> on the campus became popular, then mandatory. WWII marked the first provision of money from the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Canada" title="Government of Canada">federal government</a> to the University for research purposes. This laid a foundation for future research grants from the federal government of Canada.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Postwar_years">Postwar years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Postwar years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>By the end of World War II, Point Grey's facilities could not meet the influx of veterans returning to their studies. The university needed new staff, courses, faculties, and buildings for teaching and accommodation. The student population rose from 2,974 in 1944–45 to 9,374 in 1947–48. Surplus <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Army" title="Canadian Army">Army</a> and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Canadian_Air_Force" title="Royal Canadian Air Force">Air Force</a> camps were used for both classrooms and accommodation. The university took over fifteen complete camps during the 1945–46 session, with a sixteenth camp on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Little_Mountain_(Vancouver)" title="Little Mountain (Vancouver)">Little Mountain</a>, in Vancouver, converted into suites for married students. Most of the camps were dismantled and carried by barge or truck to the University where the huts were scattered across the campus.
</p><p>Student numbers hit 9,374 in 1948; more than 53% of the students were <a href="/wiki/Veteran" title="Veteran">war veterans</a> in 1947–67. Between 1947 and 1951, the university built twenty new permanent buildings, including the War Memorial Gym, built with money raised primarily by the students, was dedicated on October 26, 1951.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Raven-and-the-first-men.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="750" data-file-width="1000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Raven-and-the-first-men.jpg/220px-Raven-and-the-first-men.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Raven-and-the-first-men.jpg/330px-Raven-and-the-first-men.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Raven-and-the-first-men.jpg/440px-Raven-and-the-first-men.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Raven-and-the-first-men.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bill_Reid" title="Bill Reid">Bill Reid</a>'s Raven and The First Men at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UBC_Museum_of_Anthropology" title="UBC Museum of Anthropology">UBC Museum of Anthropology</a></div></div></div>
<p>The single-university policy in the West was changed as existing colleges of the provincial universities gained autonomy as universities – the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Victoria" title="University of Victoria">University of Victoria</a> was established in 1963.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_21-4"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-21">[21]</a></sup>
</p><p>On February 10, 1964 Harvey Reginald MacMillan donated $8.2 million for postgraduate education to the university.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated22_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated22-28">[28]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_history">Recent history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Recent history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Prime Minister Trudeau announced the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Anthropology_at_UBC" title="Museum of Anthropology at UBC">Museum of Anthropology</a> at UBC on July 1, 1971. At a construction cost of $2.5 million the museum building, designed by <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Erickson" title="Arthur Erickson">Arthur Erickson</a>, opened in 1976.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated22_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated22-28">[28]</a></sup> That same year, the university launched a <a href="/wiki/Normal_school" title="Normal school">normal school</a> program under the direction of <a href="/wiki/Sally_Rogow" title="Sally Rogow">Sally Rogow</a> to train educators methods to teach students with multiple disabilities or were visually impaired.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup>
</p><p>UBC's 15th president is Professor <a href="/wiki/Santa_J._Ono" title="Santa J. Ono">Santa J. Ono</a>. He assumed presidency on August 15, 2016. He served previously as the 28th President of The University of Cincinnati. Dr. Martha Piper, served as Interim President starting September 1, 2015, following the resignation of Dr. <a href="/wiki/Arvind_Gupta_(academic)" title="Arvind Gupta (academic)">Arvind Gupta</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campuses">Campuses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Campuses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UBC_aerial_view.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="407" data-file-width="500" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/UBC_aerial_view.jpg/220px-UBC_aerial_view.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/UBC_aerial_view.jpg/330px-UBC_aerial_view.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/UBC_aerial_view.jpg/440px-UBC_aerial_view.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UBC_aerial_view.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial view of the Vancouver Campus</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Irving_K._Barber_Library.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1344" data-file-width="2048" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Irving_K._Barber_Library.jpg/220px-Irving_K._Barber_Library.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Irving_K._Barber_Library.jpg/330px-Irving_K._Barber_Library.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Irving_K._Barber_Library.jpg/440px-Irving_K._Barber_Library.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Irving_K._Barber_Library.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Irving K. Barber Library and Ladner Clock Tower</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vancouver">Vancouver</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Vancouver">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Point_Grey_Campus,_University_of_British_Columbia" title="Point Grey Campus, University of British Columbia">Point Grey Campus, University of British Columbia</a></div>
<p>The main campus is at <a href="/wiki/Point_Grey" title="Point Grey">Point Grey</a>, approximately 10 kilometres (6.2 mi) from downtown Vancouver. It is near several beaches and has views of the <a href="/wiki/North_Shore_Mountains" title="North Shore Mountains">North Shore mountains</a>. The 7.63-square-kilometre (1,890-acre) <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Spirit_Regional_Park" title="Pacific Spirit Regional Park">Pacific Spirit Regional Park</a> serves as a green-belt between the campus and the city. Buildings on the Vancouver campus occupy 1.09 million m<sup>2</sup> (11.7 million sq ft) gross on 1.7 square kilometres (420 acres) of maintained land. The campus street plan is mostly in a grid of malls (some of which are pedestrian-only). Lower Mall and West Mall are in the southwestern part of the peninsula, with Main, East, and Wesbrook Malls northeast of them.
</p><p>The campus itself is situated on the unceded and traditional territory of three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_Nation" title="First Nation">First Nations</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Musqueam_Indian_Band" title="Musqueam Indian Band">xʷməθkʷəy̓əm Nation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Squamish_Nation" title="Squamish Nation">Sḵwx̱wú7mesh Úxwumixw</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tsleil-Waututh_First_Nation" title="Tsleil-Waututh First Nation">Səl̓ilw̓ətaɁɬ Nation</a>. UBC has an active partnership with xʷməθkʷəy̓əm from hən̓q̓əmin̓əm̓-language programming to a number of other classes and programmes.
</p><p>The campus is not within Vancouver's city limits, and therefore UBC is policed by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Canadian_Mounted_Police" title="Royal Canadian Mounted Police">RCMP</a> rather than the <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Police_Department" title="Vancouver Police Department">Vancouver Police Department</a>. However, the <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Fire_and_Rescue_Services" title="Vancouver Fire and Rescue Services">Vancouver Fire Department</a> provides service to UBC under a contract. In addition to UBC RCMP, there is also the UBC Campus Security that patrols the campus. Postage sent to any building on campus includes Vancouver in the address.
</p><p>UBC Vancouver also has two satellite campuses within the City of Vancouver: at <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_General_Hospital" title="Vancouver General Hospital">Vancouver General Hospital</a>, for the medical sciences, and at <a href="/wiki/Robson_Square" title="Robson Square">Robson Square</a> in downtown Vancouver, for part-time credit and non-credit programmes. UBC is also a partner in the consortium backing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Northern_Way_Campus_Ltd" title="Great Northern Way Campus Ltd">Great Northern Way Campus Ltd</a>, and is affiliated with a group of adjacent theological colleges, which include the <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_School_of_Theology" title="Vancouver School of Theology">Vancouver School of Theology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Regent_College" title="Regent College">Regent College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carey_Theological_College" title="Carey Theological College">Carey Theological College</a> and <a href="/wiki/Corpus_Christi_College_(Vancouver)" title="Corpus Christi College (Vancouver)">Corpus Christi College</a>.
</p><p>The campus is home to numerous gardens. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UBC_Botanical_Garden_and_Centre_for_Plant_Research" title="UBC Botanical Garden and Centre for Plant Research">UBC Botanical Garden and Centre for Plant Research</a>, the first UBC department, holds a collection of over 8000 different kinds of plants used for research, conservation and education. The UBC botanical garden's original site was at the "Old Arboretum". All that remains of it today are trees planted in 1916 by <a href="/wiki/John_Davidson_(botanist)" title="John Davidson (botanist)">John Davidson</a>. The old arboretum is now home to many buildings including the First Nations House of Learning. The <a href="/wiki/Nitobe_Memorial_Garden" title="Nitobe Memorial Garden">Nitobe Memorial Garden</a>, built to honour Japanese scholar <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inazo_Nitobe" title="Inazo Nitobe">Inazo Nitobe</a>, the garden has been the subject of more than fifteen years' study by a UBC professor,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (June 2012)">who?</span></a></i>]</sup> who believes its construction hides a number of impressive features, including references to Japanese philosophy and mythology, shadow bridges visible only at certain times of year, and positioning of a lantern filled with light at the exact date and time of Nitobe's death each year. The garden is behind the university's Asian Centre, which was built using steel girders from Japan's exhibit at <a href="/wiki/Expo_%2770" title="Expo '70">Osaka Expo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Library_History_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Library_History-30">[30]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vancouver_school_of_theology_(UBC-2009).JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Vancouver_school_of_theology_%28UBC-2009%29.JPG/220px-Vancouver_school_of_theology_%28UBC-2009%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Vancouver_school_of_theology_%28UBC-2009%29.JPG/330px-Vancouver_school_of_theology_%28UBC-2009%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Vancouver_school_of_theology_%28UBC-2009%29.JPG/440px-Vancouver_school_of_theology_%28UBC-2009%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vancouver_school_of_theology_(UBC-2009).JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The UBC Vancouver School of Theology building, recently acquired by the Vancouver School of Economics, built in 1927</div></div></div>
<p>The campus also features the <a href="/wiki/Chan_Centre_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Chan Centre for the Performing Arts">Chan Centre for the Performing Arts</a>: a <a href="/wiki/Performing_arts" title="Performing arts">performing arts</a> centre containing the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chan_Shun_Concert_Hall" title="Chan Shun Concert Hall">Chan Shun Concert Hall</a>, Telus Studio Theatre and the Royal Bank Cinema. It is often the site of convocation ceremonies and the filming location for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/4400_Center" title="4400 Center">4400 Center</a> on the television show <i><a href="/wiki/The_4400" title="The 4400">The 4400</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> as well as the Madacorp entrance set on <i><a href="/wiki/Kyle_XY" title="Kyle XY">Kyle XY</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> It has also been featured as the Cloud 9 Ballroom in the re-imagined <i><a href="/wiki/Battlestar_Galactica_(2004_TV_series)" title="Battlestar Galactica (2004 TV series)">Battlestar Galactica</a></i> (Season 1, Episode 11: <i>Colonial Day</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup>
</p><p>Since the mid 1980s UBC has worked with property developers to build several large residential developments throughout UBC's campus. Such developments include: Chancellor Place, Hampton Place, Hawthorn Place and Wesbrook Village.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UBC_properties_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-UBC_properties-34">[34]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Okanagan">Okanagan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Okanagan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Engineering_Management_and_Education_(UBC_Okanagan).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1552" data-file-width="2592" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Engineering_Management_and_Education_%28UBC_Okanagan%29.jpg/220px-Engineering_Management_and_Education_%28UBC_Okanagan%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Engineering_Management_and_Education_%28UBC_Okanagan%29.jpg/330px-Engineering_Management_and_Education_%28UBC_Okanagan%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Engineering_Management_and_Education_%28UBC_Okanagan%29.jpg/440px-Engineering_Management_and_Education_%28UBC_Okanagan%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Engineering_Management_and_Education_(UBC_Okanagan).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Engineering(EME) Complex at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UBC_Okanagan" title="UBC Okanagan">UBC Okanagan</a></div></div></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_University_of_British_Columbia_Okanagan" title="The University of British Columbia Okanagan">The University of British Columbia Okanagan</a></div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_British_Columbia_Okanagan" title="University of British Columbia Okanagan">Okanagan Campus</a> is a complete transformation of the site of what was once the North Kelowna Campus of <a href="/wiki/Okanagan_University_College" title="Okanagan University College">Okanagan University College</a>, next to <a href="/wiki/Kelowna_International_Airport" title="Kelowna International Airport">Kelowna International Airport</a> on the north-east side of <a href="/wiki/Kelowna" title="Kelowna">Kelowna</a>, British Columbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Its placement puts it in the <a href="/wiki/Okanagan_Nation_Alliance" title="Okanagan Nation Alliance">Okanagan Nation</a> whose lands have not been ceded to the British Columbia or Canadian governments.
</p><p>The campus offers undergraduate and graduate degrees in Arts, Science, Engineering, Nursing, Education, and Management. The Okanagan campus experienced a $450 million CDN expansion with construction of several residential, teaching and research buildings in 2011. The expansion features the Charles Fipke Centre for Innovative Research, the Engineering Management and Education building, the Arts and Science building, and the Health Science Centre. Plans to double the academic and research space are in place for the next two decades.
</p><p>In 2010, UBC Okanagan campus grew from 105 ha. to 208.6 ha.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Like the Point Grey campus, the Okanagan campus attracts Canadian and international students.
</p><p>The UBC Okanagan campus is rapidly expanding in the past decades both in student body and in research intensity and capability, and is one of the fastest growing campus among Canadian universities.
</p>
<h3><span id="Libraries.2C_archives_and_galleries"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries,_archives_and_galleries">Libraries, archives and galleries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Libraries, archives and galleries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/University_of_British_Columbia_Library" title="University of British Columbia Library">University of British Columbia Library</a></div>
<p>The UBC Library, which has 7.8 million volumes, 2.1 million e-books, more than 370,000 e-journals, and more than 700,000 items in locally produced digital collections, is Canada's second largest academic library.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-about_the_library_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-about_the_library-37">[37]</a></sup>  From 2014–2015, there were more than 3.8 million on-campus visits and over 9.5 million visits to its website.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-librarian_report_2009_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-librarian_report_2009-38">[38]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Library has fifteen branches and divisions across the UBC Vancouver and UBC Okanagan campuses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-about_the_library_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-about_the_library-37">[37]</a></sup>
</p><p>The former Main Library underwent construction and was renamed the <a href="/wiki/Irving_K._Barber_Learning_Centre" title="Irving K. Barber Learning Centre">Irving K. Barber Learning Centre</a>. Opened in April 2008, the Learning Centre incorporates the centre heritage block of the old Main Library with two new expansion wings and features an <a href="/wiki/Automated_storage_and_retrieval_system" title="Automated storage and retrieval system">automated storage and retrieval system</a> (ASRS), the first of its kind in Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup>
</p><p>UBC has a number of different collections that have been donated and acquired. Major General <a href="/wiki/Victor_Odlum" title="Victor Odlum">Victor Odlum</a> CB, CMG, DSO, VD donated his library of 10,000 books, which has been housed in "the Rockwoods Centre Library" of the UBC Library since 1963. After Videomatica's 2011 closure, UBC and SFU acquired their $1.7-million collection. UBC received about 28,000 movie DVDs, 4,000 VHS titles and 900 Blu-ray discs which are housed at UBC Library's Koerner branch on the Vancouver campus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> In 2014, renowned art collector and antiques specialist, Uno Langmann, donated the Uno Langmann Family Collection of B.C. Photographs,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> which consists of more than 18,000 rare and unique early photographs from the 1850s to the 1970s. It is considered the premiere private collection of early provincial photos, and an important illustrated history of early photographic methods. In 2016, the Library acquired one of the world's most rare and extraordinary books, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kelmscott_Chaucer" title="Kelmscott Chaucer">Kelmscott <i>Chaucer</i></a> from 1896. The book was printed in a limited edition of only 438 copies, but there are only 48 copies in the world with this particular type of binding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Morris_and_Helen_Belkin_Art_Gallery" title="Morris and Helen Belkin Art Gallery">Morris and Helen Belkin Art Gallery</a> at the UBC houses the university's collection of three archives and fine art; 1,000 works, mainly Canadian contemporary pieces 1960 to the present. The Gallery houses exhibitions, publications, acquisitions, archival projects, lectures and symposia on art history, criticism, and curating.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance_and_academics">Governance and academics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Governance and academics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Koerner_Library_UBC.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3072" data-file-width="4608" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Koerner_Library_UBC.jpg/220px-Koerner_Library_UBC.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Koerner_Library_UBC.jpg/330px-Koerner_Library_UBC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Koerner_Library_UBC.jpg/440px-Koerner_Library_UBC.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Koerner_Library_UBC.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Walter C. Koerner Library and president's office, designed by UBC alumnus <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Erickson" title="Arthur Erickson">Arthur Erickson</a></div></div></div>
<p>UBC's administration, as mandated by the University Act, is composed of a chancellor, convocation, board, senate, and faculties of the university.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-University_Act_2009-08-05_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-University_Act_2009-08-05-44">[44]</a></sup> The Board of Governors manages property and revenue, while the Senate manages the university's academic operation. Both are composed of faculty and students who are elected to the position. Degrees and diplomas are conferred by the convocation, which is composed of alumni, administrators, and faculty, with a quorum of twenty members. UBC also has a President, who is the university's chief executive officer and a member of the Senate, Board of Governors, Convocation, and also serves as Vice Chancellor. The President of the University is responsible for managing the academic operation of the university, including recommending appointments, calling meetings of faculties, and establishing committees.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculties_and_schools">Faculties and schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Faculties and schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Faculties_and_Schools_of_the_University_of_British_Columbia" title="Faculties and Schools of the University of British Columbia">Faculties and Schools of the University of British Columbia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UBC_Law_at_Allard_Hall.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2832" data-file-width="4256" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/UBC_Law_at_Allard_Hall.JPG/220px-UBC_Law_at_Allard_Hall.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/UBC_Law_at_Allard_Hall.JPG/330px-UBC_Law_at_Allard_Hall.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/UBC_Law_at_Allard_Hall.JPG/440px-UBC_Law_at_Allard_Hall.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UBC_Law_at_Allard_Hall.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial view of the UBC Faculty of Law building</div></div></div>
<p>UBC's academic activity is organized into "faculties" and "schools".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> UBC has twelve faculties at its Vancouver campus and seven at its Okanagan campus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-facts1_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-facts1-9">[9]</a></sup> UBC Vancouver has two academic colleges: Interdisciplinary Studies and Health Disciplines, while UBC Okanagan has a College of Graduate Studies. At the Vancouver campus, the Faculty of Arts, which dates back to the 1915 Fairview Campus, is the largest faculty with twenty departments and schools. With the split of the Faculty of Arts and Science in 1964, the Faculty of Science is the second largest faculty with nine departments. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sauder_School_of_Business" title="Sauder School of Business">Sauder School of Business</a> is UBC's Faculty of Commerce and Business Administration. The School of Architecture offers a program accredited by the Canadian Architectural Certification Board at the bachelor level (B.Arch.) and the master's level (M.Arch.).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> As of  December 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, a new school was created: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UBC_Vancouver_School_of_Economics" title="UBC Vancouver School of Economics">UBC Vancouver School of Economics</a> in conjunction with the Sauder School of Business.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2014, UBC created a new "International Programs" designation separate from the traditional definition of a Faculty. To accompany this designation, the university created Vantage College to allow international students who do not meet the English language requirements for general admission to enter the university's transition program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Dual undergraduate degree with Sciences Po</dt></dl>
<p>The Dual degree Program is a highly selective program in which undergraduate students earn two Bachelor of Arts degrees from both Sciences Po and UBC, or one Bachelor of Arts and one Bachelor of Commerce (Sauder School of Business) in four years. Students spend two years at one of three Sciences Po campuses in France (Le Havre, Menton, or Reims), each of which is devoted to a particular region of the world. After two years, students matriculate at UBC. Graduates are guaranteed admission to a Sciences Po graduate program. High school students may apply.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Enrollment">Enrollment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Enrollment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The mean admission average in 2013 for domestic first-year students was 89.5 percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> The acceptance rate for domestic applications in 2013 was 50.4 percent, of which 57.1 percent enrolled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup>
In 2014/15, UBC employed 3,270 full-time <a href="/wiki/Faculty_(division)" title="Faculty (division)">Faculty</a> members, 10,942 non-faculty members, and 8,031 students. It reported 871 unpaid employees.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rankings_and_reputation">Rankings and reputation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Rankings and reputation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width:23em; font-size:80%"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold"><a href="/wiki/Rankings_of_universities_in_Canada" title="Rankings of universities in Canada">University rankings</a></th></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center">Global rankings</th></tr><tr><th scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">ARWU</a></i> World<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_W_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_W-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARWUCAND_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-ARWUCAND-55">[55]</a></sup></th><td>
