3</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/Maclean%27s#University_Ranking_Guide" title="Maclean's">Maclean's</a></i> Reputation<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Macrep_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-Macrep-62">[62]</a></sup></th><td>
2</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>UBC has the second highest average entering grade among Canadian universities, with an average undergraduate entrance grade of 89.6%, only behind <a href="/wiki/McGill_University" title="McGill University">McGill University</a> with 90.3%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Josh_Dehaas_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Josh_Dehaas-63">[63]</a></sup> In the 2019 <i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a></i> UBC was ranked second in Canada, 37th overall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_THES_W_57-2"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_THES_W-57">[57]</a></sup> The 2018 <i><a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a></i> ranked the university second in Canada, and 43rd overall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_W_54-2"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_W-54">[54]</a></sup> The University was ranked 3rd in Canada, and 47th among world universities in the 2019 <i><a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QS_56-2"><a href="#cite_note-QS-56">[56]</a></sup> In the 2018 <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._News_and_World_Report" title="U.S. News and World Report">U.S. News and World Report</a></i> ranking of world universities UBC placed second in Canada, and 27th overall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USNWR_Best_Global_Universities_60-2"><a href="#cite_note-USNWR_Best_Global_Universities-60">[60]</a></sup> UBC was ranked 3rd in Canada among all its major/research universities in the <i><a href="/wiki/Maclean%27s" title="Maclean's">Maclean's</a></i> 24th annual rankings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Macdoc_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-Macdoc-61">[61]</a></sup> In <i><a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s 2011 global university rankings, the university was ranked eighth among institutions outside the United States, and second in Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thedailybeast.com_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-thedailybeast.com-64">[64]</a></sup> As of  September 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, according to the <i><a href="/wiki/University_Ranking_by_Academic_Performance" title="University Ranking by Academic Performance">University Ranking by Academic Performance</a></i> (URAP),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> UBC was ranked second in Canada, 16th in North America and 21st in the world.
</p><p>The 2016 <i>QS World University Rankings</i> ranked UBC 5th worldwide in geography, 9th in education, 15th in agriculture and forestry, 17th in psychology, 20th in nursing, 24th in mathematics, 26th in English literature, 28th in both economics and medicine, 36th in sociology, 37th in political science and 39th in accounting and finance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> The 2014–2015 <i>Times Higher Education World University Rankings</i> ranked UBC 20th (1st in Canada) in life sciences, 21st (2nd in Canada) in social sciences, 35th (2nd in Canada) in physical sciences and 43rd (2nd in Canada) in engineering and technology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> The 2014 <i>Academic Ranking of World Universities</i> ranked UBC 28th in social sciences, 38th in economics and business, 41st in computer science and 51–75 overall in science.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> The university's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_British_Columbia_Faculty_of_Law" title="University of British Columbia Faculty of Law">law faculty</a> was ranked fifth in <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maclean" title="Maclean">Maclean</a>'s</i> 2012 rankings of Canadian <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">common law</a> schools, and 22nd in the world and third in Canada in the 2012 <i>QS World University Rankings</i> by Subject: Law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sauder_School_of_Business" title="Sauder School of Business">Sauder School of Business</a> has also received national and international accolades. The business school appeared on the 2013 <i><a href="/wiki/Financial_Times" title="Financial Times">Financial Times</a></i> global MBA rankings, placing 57th in the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> and fourth in Canada. The business school was also ranked in QS's 2012 North American MBA rankings, placing 18th in North America, and third in Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chan_centre_performing_arts_concert_tessler.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1100" data-file-width="870" height="278" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Chan_centre_performing_arts_concert_tessler.jpg/220px-Chan_centre_performing_arts_concert_tessler.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Chan_centre_performing_arts_concert_tessler.jpg/330px-Chan_centre_performing_arts_concert_tessler.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Chan_centre_performing_arts_concert_tessler.jpg/440px-Chan_centre_performing_arts_concert_tessler.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chan_centre_performing_arts_concert_tessler.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Chan_Centre_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Chan Centre for the Performing Arts">Chan Centre for the Performing Arts</a>, designed by <a href="/wiki/Bing_Thom" title="Bing Thom">Bing Thom</a>, B.Arch '66</div></div></div>
<p>The University of British Columbia is a member of <a href="/wiki/Universitas_21" title="Universitas 21">Universitas 21</a>, an international association of research-led institutions and the only Canadian member of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Pacific_Rim_Universities" title="Association of Pacific Rim Universities">Association of Pacific Rim Universities</a>, a consortium of 42 leading research universities in the Pacific Rim.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-universitas_21_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-universitas_21-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-apru_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-apru-74">[74]</a></sup> With a sponsored research income of $575.155 million, the university manages the second-largest <a href="/wiki/Funding_of_science" title="Funding of science">research budget</a> of any university in Canada. With an average research income of $245,200 CAD per full-time faculty member, the university is also the country's second most research intensive full-service university.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup>
</p><p>In terms of research performance, High Impact Universities 2010 ranked the university 30th out of 500 universities, and second in Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Higher_Education_Evaluation_and_Accreditation_Council_of_Taiwan" title="Higher Education Evaluation and Accreditation Council of Taiwan">Higher Education Evaluation and Accreditation Council of Taiwan</a> (HEEACT), an organization which also evaluates universities based on their scientific paper's performances, ranked the university 29th in the world and second in Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup>
</p><p>The university operates and manages a number of research centres:
</p>
<ul><li>In 1972, a consortium of the University of British Columbia and four other universities from Alberta and British Columbia established the <a href="/wiki/Bamfield_Marine_Sciences_Centre" title="Bamfield Marine Sciences Centre">Bamfield Marine Sciences Centre</a>. Located on Vancouver Island, the centre provides year-round research facilities and technical assistance for biologists, ecologists and oceanographers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Peter_Wall_Institute_for_Advanced_Studies" title="Peter Wall Institute for Advanced Studies">Peter Wall Institute for Advanced Studies</a> is an interdisciplinary research institute for fundamental research in the Sciences, Social Sciences, and Humanities.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/UBC_Farm" title="UBC Farm">UBC Farm</a> is a 24 hectare learning and research farm in UBC's South Campus area. It features Saturday Farm Markets from early June until early October, selling organic produce and eggs to the community.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/TRIUMF" title="TRIUMF">TRIUMF</a>, a laboratory specializing in <a href="/wiki/Particle_physics" title="Particle physics">particle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_physics" title="Nuclear physics">nuclear physics</a> is also at the university. The name was formerly an acronym for TRI-University Meson Facility, but TRIUMF is now owned and operated by a consortium of eleven Canadian universities. The consortium runs TRIUMF through a contribution of funds from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Research_Council_of_Canada" title="National Research Council of Canada">National Research Council of Canada</a>, and makes TRIUMF's facilities available to Canadian scientists and to scientists from around the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sustainability">Sustainability</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Sustainability">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>UBC has been ranked in the <a href="/wiki/Corporate_Knights" title="Corporate Knights">Corporate Knights</a> school rankings, which ranks universities based on how well they integrate sustainability into the learning experience. The rankings adopt a broad definition of sustainability which encompasses both environmental and social concerns. In the 2011 rankings, UBC was ranked 2nd in the category: top 5 teaching programs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CorpK_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-CorpK-80">[80]</a></sup> UBC's law school ranked fifth among Canadian law schools.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CorpK_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-CorpK-80">[80]</a></sup> The Sauder School of Business' MBA programs were ranked fourth in Canada. The same rankings placed the business school 11th in Canada for its undergraduate business program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CorpK_80-2"><a href="#cite_note-CorpK-80">[80]</a></sup>
</p><p>The university strives to be a world leader in sustainability and sustainable development, aiming to meet the needs of the growing student and faculty population while preserving the environment. The Center for Interactive Research on Sustainability (CIRS) building, a recent addition to the Vancouver campus, exemplifies the University's sustainable practices. Developed to create the most sustainable society at UBC, it has been called North America's most sustainable, innovative, and high performance building.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HoldenM_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-HoldenM-81">[81]</a></sup>
</p><p>The CIRS building was first thought of in 2000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIRS_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-CIRS-82">[82]</a></sup> and was the brainchild of John Robinson, a sustainable development research initiative professor. Robinson worked with faculty members from Emily Carr, Simon Fraser University, and British Columbia Institute of Technology as well as head architect Peter Busby to design the building.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PlummerR_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-PlummerR-83">[83]</a></sup> It cost 23 million dollars to complete the 65,000 square foot building.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BulaF_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-BulaF-84">[84]</a></sup>
</p><p>The CIRS building exhibits regenerative sustainability, which means the building improves the surrounding environment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RobinsonJ_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-RobinsonJ-85">[85]</a></sup>  For example, it uses energy it obtains from the neighbouring Earth and Ocean Sciences (EOSC) Building to heat itself. The EOSC building uses roughly 1600 megawatts of heat energy and goes through ten air changes every hour, which wastes around 900 megawatts of energy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIRS_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-CIRS-82">[82]</a></sup> The engineers who built the CIRS building saw this as an opportunity; the building takes the heat the EOSC building expels and uses 300 megawatts to heat itself before returning 600 megawatts to the EOSC building. In this way, the CIRS building restores its surrounding environment.
</p><p>The CIRS building is designed to be net positive in four ways environmentally, meaning the processes or products that leave the building are more environmentally friendly than those that go into it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HoldenM_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-HoldenM-81">[81]</a></sup> The best example of the building's net positivity is the building's wood holds nearly 600 tons of carbon – more carbon than the building's construction and maintenance created.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SuzukiD_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-SuzukiD-86">[86]</a></sup>
Other sustainable features of the CIRS building include:
</p>
<ul><li>A water supply obtained entirely from rainwater</li>
<li>An on-site sewage treatment facility that converts all waste created in the building to reusable water and compost</li>
<li>The building's wood comes from trees killed by the pine beetle, thus, little logging was needed for construction</li>
<li>Relies on mainly solar energy for electricity</li>
<li>All areas of the building use natural lighting during the day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HoldenM_81-2"><a href="#cite_note-HoldenM-81">[81]</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>The building integrates 'green' sustainable and humane features, i.e. not only does it have a small ecological footprint, it also serves as an environment for occupants to be happy, healthy, and productive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PlummerR_83-1"><a href="#cite_note-PlummerR-83">[83]</a></sup> This is the direction the University of British Columbia is moving towards to continue their ideas of sustainable development.
</p><p>Following the success of the CIRS, UBC's new Student Union Building, which opened in summer 2015, was also designed to adhere to the most stringent sustainability requirements. It achieves the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LEED_Platinum" title="LEED Platinum">LEED Platinum</a> standard – with features that include triple glazing, solar-powered cooling, solar water heaters, radiant heating and cooling in floors, <a href="/wiki/Green_roof" title="Green roof">green roof</a> technology, water efficient landscaping that uses <a href="/wiki/Greywater" title="Greywater">greywater</a>, natural air ventilation, and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Composting" title="Composting">composting</a> facility that processes up to 30 tonnes of organic waste each year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vancitysub_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-vancitysub-87">[87]</a></sup>
</p><p>Canada has the highest water consumption per capita in the world, and Vancouver having the highest population in British Columbia, water consumption is significantly high.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> The water consumption in the University of British Columbia in Vancouver is significantly high due UBC being the largest university in British Columbia. Due to the high population, the consumption of water sums up to about four billion litres a year, able to fill 1,600 Olympic-sized swimming pools.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_Action_Plan">Water Action Plan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Water Action Plan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>To implement change in the water consumption, UBC sustainability team created an initiative to conserve called the Water Action Plan in 2011 in hopes to reduce and recycle water on campus. Two landmarks for creating water sustainability are the CIRS and the C. K. Choi Building. The Centre for Interactive Sustainability (CIRS) building features a closed loop water system where water is recycled and reused. On the other hand, the C. K. Choi Building for the Institute of Asian Research, consists of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Composting_toilets" title="Composting toilets">composting toilets</a>, which reduce domestic water consumption. These toilets use an alternative other than using water for flushing and produce fertilizer that can be used for growing plants. Conclusively, these toilets allow for conservation of water, landfill space, energy, and also production of quality fertilizer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_conservation_initiatives">Water conservation initiatives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Water conservation initiatives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>For over 20 years, UBC has been implementing change and water consumption policies through two initiatives, ECOTrek and UBC Renew:
</p>
<ul><li>ECOTrek
<dl><dd>ECOTrek is Canada's largest sustainability project which undertook an enormous water and energy saving initiative. This project included rebuilding almost 300 academic buildings in UBC. This project achieved a World Clean Energy nomination, which are honorable awards for successful projects in energy efficiency and renewable energy realm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> The water management involved conducting changes to toilets, urinals, basins and water-cooled equipment to reduce the amount of water on campus. In addition, steam and water meters were installed on campus to quantify the water consumption to provide a clear depiction of the water use in each building.</dd></dl></li>
<li>UBC Renew
<dl><dd>UBC Renew project involves renovating aging institutional buildings, instead of demolishing and building new buildings which can have negative impacts on the environment. <a href="/wiki/Demolition" title="Demolition">Demolition</a> can have major environmental impacts as it can pollute the soil, increase air pollutants, and increase water consumption. Renovating old buildings can save large volumes of water and save energy costs.</dd></dl></li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Community_efforts">Community efforts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Community efforts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Beyond the UBC sustainability team, a student-driven initiative is taking place in making a bottled-water free campus in hopes of reducing <a href="/wiki/Bottled_water" title="Bottled water">bottled water</a> on campus and to encourage students to engage in environmentally friendly behaviours. Production of bottled water puts strain on the environment and increases landfill space. According to the World Wide Fund for Nature 2001 report, about 1.5 million tons of plastic is used for bottling 89 billion litres of water each year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Indigenous">Indigenous</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Indigenous">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>UBC's Longhouse is the University's centre for <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Canada" title="Indigenous peoples in Canada">Indigenous</a> activities. The university has an Associate Dean of Indigenous Education, and has developed governing board and senate policies as well as Aboriginal governed councils within the university structure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> UBC offers degrees in First Nations and Indigenous Studies<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> through a program in the Arts Faculty, and a Chinook Diploma Program in the Sauder School of Business; it also runs the Chinook Summer Biz Camp, to foster entrepreneurship among First Nations and Métis high school students.  It hosts a Bridge Through Sport Program, Summer Science Program, Native Youth Program, and Cedar Day Camp and Afterschool Program.  Its First Nations Forestry Initiatives were developed in partnership with specific Aboriginal communities to meet needs in their more remote areas.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Finances">Finances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Finances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2012–13, UBC's budget exceeded $2 billion, and the University posted balanced financial results for the fourth consecutive year through strategic revenue diversification, careful management of assets, and a continued focus on fundraising for projects across the university. The share of the University budget coming from the Government grant has been reduced to 45% of total revenues. On the other hand, annual fundraising has nearly doubled in 5 years to reach $213 million.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tuition">Tuition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Tuition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tuition" title="Tuition">Tuition fees</a> vary significantly between Canadian citizens (and permanent residents) and international students. In addition, for both undergraduate and graduate programs, tuition rates vary among the university's faculties. Students must also pay for various living expenses such as housing, food and health care. As of the 2012–2013 school year, these expenses were estimated at around $13,000 CAD per academic year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Undergraduate_tuition">Undergraduate tuition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Undergraduate tuition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>UBC tuition for 2012 was $4,700 before adding other mandatory administrative fees for a Canadian student in a basic 30-unit program, though various programs cost from $3,406 to $9,640. Tuition for international students is significantly higher (2.3–4.6 times higher than domestic students). In 2012, tuition for international students ranged from $16,245 CAD to $25,721 CAD.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2001–02, UBC had one of the lowest undergraduate tuition rates in Canada, at an average of $2,181 CAD per year for a full-time programme due to a government-instituted tuition freeze.
</p><p>In 2001, the BC Liberal party defeated the NDP in British Columbia and lifted the tuition freeze. In 2002–03 undergraduate and graduate tuition rose by an average of 30%, and up to 40% in some faculties. This has led to better facilities, but also to <a href="/wiki/Student_activism" title="Student activism">student unrest</a> and contributed to a teaching assistant <a href="/wiki/Strike_action" title="Strike action">union strike</a>.
</p><p>UBC again increased tuition by 30% in the 2003–04 year, again by approximately 15% in the 2004–05 season, and 2% in the 2005–06 and 2006–07 years. Increases were lower than expected because, in the 2005 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Speech_from_the_Throne" title="Speech from the Throne">Speech from the Throne</a>, the government announced tuition increases would be capped to inflation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> In 2006–07, the Canadian average undergraduate tuition fee was $4,347 and the BC average was $4,960.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> In 2014, the Board of Governor passed a one-time 10% tuition increase for all new incoming International students.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> In December 2015, UBC's Board of Governors passed a motion increasing international tuition by more than 46.8% for the academic years 2016–17, 2017–18, 2018–2019. This announcement was met with indignation by many of the University's students as this was the second major increase in international tuition in less than a year, taking total international student tuition fee increases to above 60% within 4 years (minimum international tuition will be benchmarked at $35,071 CAD in the year 2018–19).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Graduate_tuition">Graduate tuition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Graduate tuition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the academic year 2011/2012 most research-based graduate programs assess tuition of $4,263.87 per semester for Canadian students and permanent residents or $7,490.88 for international students.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> International students without external funding that meet the general eligibility criteria will be supported with guaranteed funding of up to $3,200 per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> Tuition for professional Master's programs varies.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_representation">Student representation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Student representation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alma_Mater_Society_of_the_University_of_British_Columbia" title="Alma Mater Society of the University of British Columbia">Alma Mater Society of the University of British Columbia</a>, or AMS, represents UBC undergraduate students within the Vancouver campus. The society's mandate is to improve the quality of educational, social, and personal lives of UBC students. The AMS lobbies the UBC administration on behalf of the student body, provides services such as the AMS/GSS Health and Dental Plan, supports and administers student clubs, and maintains the Student Union Building (aka SUB) and the services it houses. A Constituency (undergraduate society) exists within each schools and faculties of the university and act as the subsidiary of the AMS within those schools and faculties.
</p><p>The Graduate Student Society (GSS), which operates as an independent entity, represents graduate students. A council representing each graduate program and an executive elected by graduate students as a whole governs the GSS.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup>
</p><p>The university also allows elected student representatives to sit as voting members in the Board of Governors (3 student representatives) and the Academic Senate. Although the university is the official body that elects the students, the university delegates these representative elections to the AMS.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_facilities">Student facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Student facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_Student_Union_Building_of_the_University_of_British_Columbia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2560" data-file-width="7920" height="71" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/New_Student_Union_Building_of_the_University_of_British_Columbia.jpg/220px-New_Student_Union_Building_of_the_University_of_British_Columbia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/New_Student_Union_Building_of_the_University_of_British_Columbia.jpg/330px-New_Student_Union_Building_of_the_University_of_British_Columbia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/New_Student_Union_Building_of_the_University_of_British_Columbia.jpg/440px-New_Student_Union_Building_of_the_University_of_British_Columbia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_Student_Union_Building_of_the_University_of_British_Columbia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The new Student Union Building, which opened in 2015.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Interior_of_the_UBC_Student_Union_Building_13.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4909" data-file-width="6216" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Interior_of_the_UBC_Student_Union_Building_13.jpg/220px-Interior_of_the_UBC_Student_Union_Building_13.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Interior_of_the_UBC_Student_Union_Building_13.jpg/330px-Interior_of_the_UBC_Student_Union_Building_13.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Interior_of_the_UBC_Student_Union_Building_13.jpg/440px-Interior_of_the_UBC_Student_Union_Building_13.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Interior_of_the_UBC_Student_Union_Building_13.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The interior of the new Student Union Building contains a "bird's nest" where students may relax and study.</div></div></div>
<p>The heart of student activity at UBC Vancouver is the centrally located Student Union Building (SUB), which houses offices of many AMS student clubs, over a dozen restaurants and cafés, a pub ("The Gallery"), a nightclub ("The Pit"), the 425-seat Norman Bouchard Memorial Theatre ("The Norm Theatre"), several shops, and a post office. The AMS runs the majority of the SUB's outlets and shops; however, UBC Food Services' recent addition of major corporate outlets has generated controversy. The SUB Art Gallery contains mostly students' works. An underground bus loop to replace the "Grassy Knoll" beside the SUB did not receive funding by <a href="/wiki/TransLink_(British_Columbia)" title="TransLink (British Columbia)">Translink</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bus_Loop_Letter_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bus_Loop_Letter-107">[107]</a></sup>
As a result, the administration has cancelled the bus loop project, although the rest of the renovations of the University Boulevard Neighbourhood are still under consideration.
</p><p>In June 2015, the new Student Union Building—called the AMS Student Nest or simply the "Nest"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup>—opened to students, largely replacing and extending the old SUB in functionality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vancitysub_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-vancitysub-87">[87]</a></sup> The Nest, built for $107 million, is much larger than its predecessor, and has numerous amenities including a performance centre, an art exhibition space, a large ballroom, a three-storey climbing wall, radio broadcast facilities, a daycare, and a 10,740 square foot rooftop garden and public space with a water feature and outdoor seating. Many of the restaurants as well as the Pit Pub have moved to the Nest under their original name or with new names.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vancitysub_87-2"><a href="#cite_note-vancitysub-87">[87]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UBC_Bookstore_2015.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3345" data-file-width="5352" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/UBC_Bookstore_2015.jpg/220px-UBC_Bookstore_2015.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/UBC_Bookstore_2015.jpg/330px-UBC_Bookstore_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/UBC_Bookstore_2015.jpg/440px-UBC_Bookstore_2015.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UBC_Bookstore_2015.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Exterior of the main UBC Bookstore.</div></div></div>
<p>Other student facilities on campus include the Ladha Science Student Centre (funded through a donation from Abdul Ladha, a levy on Science undergraduate students, the VP Students, and the Dean of Science) and the Meekison Arts Student Space in the Faculty of Art's Buchanan D building. The UBC Bookstore's locations on the Vancouver campus: the main store at 6200 University Boulevard and a store at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sauder_School_of_Business" title="Sauder School of Business">Sauder School of Business</a> join the stores at the Okanagan and Robson Square Campuses in offering a variety of products and services. The bookstores return a dividend to UBC each year, which is re-invested in the campus or in student and community organizations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greek_organizations">Greek organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Greek organizations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>While UBC's Greek system is somewhat smaller than its counterparts in the United States, UBC's 18 Greek organizations make up Canada's largest and most active Greek system. The Alma Mater Society recognizes an InterFraternal Council (IFC) as a club, and weekly meetings of the fraternities under IFC take place at their respective fraternity houses. Greek life has its own division within UBC REC<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> and intense competition between the nine Fraternities for the title of top Athletic Fraternity occur.
</p><p>There are ten international fraternities on campus, the first of which was <a href="/wiki/Zeta_Psi" title="Zeta Psi">Zeta Psi</a>, in January 1926. Although its disputed, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Delta_Phi" title="Alpha Delta Phi">Alpha Delta Phi</a> soon came to campus and chartered 3 months later. However, Zeta Psi and Alpha Delta Phi were preceded by several local fraternities on campus. Other fraternities include <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Epsilon_Pi" title="Alpha Epsilon Pi">Alpha Epsilon Pi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Kappa_Epsilon" title="Delta Kappa Epsilon">Delta Kappa Epsilon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Psi_Upsilon" title="Psi Upsilon">Psi Upsilon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Chi" title="Sigma Chi">Sigma Chi</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sigma_Chi_UBC_-_Delta_Omicron_chapter_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sigma_Chi_UBC_-_Delta_Omicron_chapter-111">[111]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Beta_Theta_Pi" title="Beta Theta Pi">Beta Theta Pi</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Phi_Delta_Theta" title="Phi Delta Theta">Phi Delta Theta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phi_Gamma_Delta" title="Phi Gamma Delta">Phi Gamma Delta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Sigma" title="Kappa Sigma">Kappa Sigma</a>, and Zeta Psi, which re-chartered at UBC in 2013.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Panhellenic_Conference" title="National Panhellenic Conference">National Panhellenic Conference</a> (NPC) member organizations (sororities) on campus are overseen by the Panhellenic Council.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> All sororities have a chapter room in the Panhellenic House on Wesbrook Mall; the building also offers housing for 72 college women, with preference given to sorority members.
</p><p>The eight sororities on the Vancouver campus include <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Delta_Pi" title="Alpha Delta Pi">Alpha Delta Pi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Gamma_Delta" title="Alpha Gamma Delta">Alpha Gamma Delta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Omicron_Pi" title="Alpha Omicron Pi">Alpha Omicron Pi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Phi" title="Alpha Phi">Alpha Phi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Gamma" title="Delta Gamma">Delta Gamma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gamma_Phi_Beta" title="Gamma Phi Beta">Gamma Phi Beta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Alpha_Theta" title="Kappa Alpha Theta">Kappa Alpha Theta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Kappa_Gamma" title="Kappa Kappa Gamma">Kappa Kappa Gamma</a>. The current Panhellenic total is 104. Chapter meetings are held in the chapter's respective rooms each week or in classrooms and Greek-wide or campus-wide events are attended by members of all the sororities and fraternities. Formal recruitment for the sororities begin during the second week of September and is a 4-day process consisting of: Tours (first 2 days), Invitationals and Preference.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Phrateres" title="Phrateres">Phrateres</a> has traditionally been affiliated with the Greek system since its installation at UBC in 1935. Historical records indicate that for many years, members identified themselves, and were recognized as Greek. Members interacted with fraternities on a similar basis as the sororities, and participated in many Greek events, such as Songfest and exchanges. However, they presently operate as a self-governing organization under the Alma Mater Society with the closure of their international headquarters in 2001.
</p><p>Both campuses also have chapters of <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Phi_Delta" title="Sigma Phi Delta">Sigma Phi Delta</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Omega_Epsilon" title="Alpha Omega Epsilon">Alpha Omega Epsilon</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> a professional engineering fraternity and sorority respectively. None of the four chapters are affiliated with the other Greek organizations on campus.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Alpha_Kappa_Psi" title="Alpha Kappa Psi">Alpha Kappa Psi</a> (professional business fraternity) too has an active chapter at UBC since 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> It consists of students from all faculty. They do not have a house and are not affiliated with any other Greek organization on campus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Alpha_Phi_Omega" title="Alpha Phi Omega">Alpha Phi Omega</a> (Community service fraternity) founded its first chapter in Canada at UBC in 2015.
</p><p>Moreover, UBC was ranked among Canada's top <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Party_schools" title="Party schools">party schools</a> by the website <i>Ask Men</i>. In the latest ranking, UBC was ranked 7th, ahead of <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_University" title="Queen's University">Queen's University</a> and below <a href="/wiki/Concordia_University" title="Concordia University">Concordia University</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Residences">Residences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Residences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gage_residence.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="563" data-file-width="863" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Gage_residence.jpg/220px-Gage_residence.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Gage_residence.jpg/330px-Gage_residence.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Gage_residence.jpg/440px-Gage_residence.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gage_residence.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gage Towers</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dene_Totem_Park.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Dene_Totem_Park.JPG/220px-Dene_Totem_Park.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Dene_Totem_Park.JPG/330px-Dene_Totem_Park.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Dene_Totem_Park.JPG/440px-Dene_Totem_Park.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dene_Totem_Park.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Totem Park, Dene House</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Marine_Drive_Residence.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Marine_Drive_Residence.JPG/220px-Marine_Drive_Residence.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Marine_Drive_Residence.JPG/330px-Marine_Drive_Residence.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Marine_Drive_Residence.JPG/440px-Marine_Drive_Residence.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Marine_Drive_Residence.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Marine Drive</div></div></div>
<p>The UBC Point Grey campus has a resident population of about 10,041 students <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> who live in an <a href="/wiki/Unincorporated_area" title="Unincorporated area">unincorporated area</a>, outside the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/City_of_Vancouver" title="City of Vancouver">City of Vancouver</a> known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Vancouver_Electoral_Area_A" title="Greater Vancouver Electoral Area A">Electoral Area A</a> within and partly administered by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metro_Vancouver" title="Metro Vancouver">Metro Vancouver</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> Neighbouring the <a href="/wiki/University_Endowment_Lands" title="University Endowment Lands">University Endowment Lands</a>, on-campus residential services are provided by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Province_of_British_Columbia" title="Province of British Columbia">Province of BC</a> and by UBC. Emergency Planning is administered by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metro_Vancouver" title="Metro Vancouver">Metro Vancouver</a>. Because UBC is not in a municipality, there is no mayor, council, or other democratic municipal representation for on-campus residents, although residents can vote for the Director of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Vancouver_Electoral_Area_A" title="Greater Vancouver Electoral Area A">Electoral Area A</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> British Columbia's Residential Tenancy Act does not protect UBC residents because university accommodations for students and employees are exempt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup>
</p><p>UBC has forecast the need for 6,400 new on-campus beds between 2008 and 2028 "to maintain the current availability of student housing choices in the face of on-going pressures in the Vancouver rental market".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> From 2009 to 2014, UBC added 1,471 beds for student residents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> In 2015, UBC plans to increase the cost of on-campus student housing by 20%, with the exception of year-round residences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup>
</p><p>As of the 2017–2018 school year, there are three <a href="/wiki/Dormitory" title="Dormitory">dormitory</a> style residences on campus, primarily for first and second-year students: Totem Park, Place Vanier, and Orchard Commons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup>
</p><p>Totem Park, housing about 2,129 students, consists of nine dormitory buildings (Nootka, Dene, Haida, Salish, Kwakiutl, Shuswap, Həm'ləsəm', Q'ələχən, Building 7), and a Commons Block (Coquihalla). All houses, except Shuswap and Building 7, are co-ed, with alternating men's and women's floors; Shuswap house and Building 7 has co-ed floors. Həm'ləsəm' and Q'ələχən houses were opened to Totem Park residents in September 2011 and have single rooms with semi-private or private washrooms in contrast to the other houses' communal floor washrooms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> Building 7 was opened to Totem Park residents in September 2017 and has single rooms with communal bathrooms.
</p><p>Place Vanier, housing 1,370 people, consists of 12 blocks constructed in 1959 (Robson House), 1960 (Okanagan, Sherwood Lett, Mackenzie, Ross, Hamber, and Mawdsley Houses), 1961 (Kootenay House), 1968 (Cariboo and Tweedsmuir Houses), 2002 (Korea-UBC House) and 2003 (Tec de Monterrey-UBC House). The buildings vary from male and female only, to alternating gender floors, as well as fully mixed floors. The residences have single and double rooms, and each floor has a lounge and communal bathrooms.
</p><p>Orchard Commons consists of two apartment style buildings, Braeburn house and Bartlett house, with the latter containing a common dining hall and reception area. Orchard Commons houses 1,047 students, with the majority staying in connected single rooms on mixed gender floors, where two same-gender residents share a washroom connecting their adjacent rooms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup>
</p><p>Students nineteen and older have suite-style residence options on the Point Grey campus. The <a href="/wiki/Walter_Gage" title="Walter Gage">Gage</a> Towers consist of three 17-floor towers (North, South and East) primarily for second, third, and fourth-year undergraduate students. It consists of three interconnected towers (North, South, and East) as well as single student housing (both studio, and apartment) in a building. The towers are composed of "quads": four separate pods, each consisting of six individual bedrooms, a bathroom and a kitchen-dining area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup>
</p><p>Acadia Park and University Apartments are for student families and couples (where one is a UBC student) and are administered on a year-round basis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup>
</p><p>Next to the Acadia Park residence area on the east part of campus is Fairview Crescent, a residence primarily for second- and third-year undergraduate students and many graduate students. The residence consists of an L-shaped pedestrian-only street lined with 4, 5 and six-student (a mix of single-sex and co-ed) townhouses. The Beanery coffee shop is in the middle of the residence. Within a 5-minute walk from Fairview Crescent is the Fraser Hall residence which houses approximately 200 students. Fairview Crescent and Fraser Hall are both governed by the Fairview and Fraser Residence Association.
</p><p>The Thunderbird residences are primarily for graduate students and fourth-year undergraduate students; they are at the academic core campus' southern edge. The Ritsumeikan-UBC House is a residence with a Japanese cultural setting, named for <a href="/wiki/Ritsumeikan_University" title="Ritsumeikan University">Ritsumeikan University</a>. It houses Japanese exchange students and Canadian students, who participate in unique inter-cultural programmes. UBC's <a href="/wiki/Urasenke" title="Urasenke">Urasenke</a> <a href="/wiki/Japanese_tea_ceremony" title="Japanese tea ceremony">Japanese tea ceremony</a> club uses the residence's <a href="/wiki/Tatami" title="Tatami">tatami</a> room for practice sessions. Two Canadian students are typically paired with two Japanese exchange students.
</p><p>Marine Drive Residence is on the west side of campus, slightly south of Place Vanier. The first phase, consisting of Building 1 (an 18-floor tower) and Building 2 (a five-floor building commonly called the "Podium") opened in fall 2005. In February 2006, the Board of Governors approved plans for Marine Drive's second phase, putting an end to the debacle caused by concerns over the view of Wreck beach (Phase I's Building 1 was reduced from 20 floors to 18). Additionally, building 1 contains the Simon K.Y. Lee Global Lounge and Resource Centre. Phase II consists of Buildings 4 through 6 (two towers and another "Podium", respectively), and also the Commonsblock. Buildings 4 through 6 were all open to students as of  September 2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>. A separate Commonsblock was completed in summer 2009, and has similar services to the Commonsblock of other residences, such as exercise, game, and study rooms. Construction at Marine Drive was completed in February 2010, with the opening of The Point Grill restaurant in Building 4.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ponderosa_Studios_at_the_University_of_British_Columbia_2016.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3660" data-file-width="6771" height="119" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Ponderosa_Studios_at_the_University_of_British_Columbia_2016.jpg/220px-Ponderosa_Studios_at_the_University_of_British_Columbia_2016.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Ponderosa_Studios_at_the_University_of_British_Columbia_2016.jpg/330px-Ponderosa_Studios_at_the_University_of_British_Columbia_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Ponderosa_Studios_at_the_University_of_British_Columbia_2016.jpg/440px-Ponderosa_Studios_at_the_University_of_British_Columbia_2016.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ponderosa_Studios_at_the_University_of_British_Columbia_2016.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ponderosa Commons, Oak House</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Orchard_Commons_at_the_University_of_British_Columbia_2016.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="7366" data-file-width="4920" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Orchard_Commons_at_the_University_of_British_Columbia_2016.jpg/170px-Orchard_Commons_at_the_University_of_British_Columbia_2016.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Orchard_Commons_at_the_University_of_British_Columbia_2016.jpg/255px-Orchard_Commons_at_the_University_of_British_Columbia_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Orchard_Commons_at_the_University_of_British_Columbia_2016.jpg/340px-Orchard_Commons_at_the_University_of_British_Columbia_2016.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Orchard_Commons_at_the_University_of_British_Columbia_2016.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Orchard Commons, Braeburn House</div></div></div>
<p>The newest additions to UBC Vancouver's student housing are the Ponderosa Commons and Orchard Commons residences, completed in 2016, and Brock Commons, opened in the Summer of 2017.
</p><p>The university has two colleges to accommodate graduate students, postdoctoral fellows and visiting scholars: St. John's College<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Green_College,_University_of_British_Columbia" title="Green College, University of British Columbia">Green College</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup>
</p><p>Brock Commons Tallwood House opened in 2017, becoming the tallest mass wood building in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Olympic_Hockey_at_UBC.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="576" data-file-width="1024" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Olympic_Hockey_at_UBC.jpg/220px-Olympic_Hockey_at_UBC.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Olympic_Hockey_at_UBC.jpg/330px-Olympic_Hockey_at_UBC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Olympic_Hockey_at_UBC.jpg/440px-Olympic_Hockey_at_UBC.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Olympic_Hockey_at_UBC.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>UBC's Doug Mitchell Thunderbird Sports Centre during the <a href="/wiki/2010_Winter_Olympics" title="2010 Winter Olympics">2010 Winter Olympics</a></div></div></div>
<p>The University of British Columbia's sports teams are called the <a href="/wiki/UBC_Thunderbirds" title="UBC Thunderbirds">Thunderbirds</a>. The Thunderbirds participate in the <a href="/wiki/U_Sports" title="U Sports">U Sports</a> <a href="/wiki/Canada_West_Universities_Athletic_Association" title="Canada West Universities Athletic Association">Canada West Universities Athletic Association</a> for most varsity sports. However, several varsity teams at UBC compete in the <a href="/wiki/National_Association_of_Intercollegiate_Athletics" title="National Association of Intercollegiate Athletics">National Association of Intercollegiate Athletics</a>. UBC is considering joining the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NCAA" title="NCAA">NCAA</a> <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_II" title="NCAA Division II">Division II</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> With a long history of competing in sports, the Thunderbirds have garnered a number of championships. In particular, the women swimmers who had represented UBC had brought back 22 conference championships and 16 national championships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Indoor_climbing_at_the_UBC_Student_Union_Building.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4912" data-file-width="7360" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Indoor_climbing_at_the_UBC_Student_Union_Building.jpg/220px-Indoor_climbing_at_the_UBC_Student_Union_Building.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Indoor_climbing_at_the_UBC_Student_Union_Building.jpg/330px-Indoor_climbing_at_the_UBC_Student_Union_Building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Indoor_climbing_at_the_UBC_Student_Union_Building.jpg/440px-Indoor_climbing_at_the_UBC_Student_Union_Building.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Indoor_climbing_at_the_UBC_Student_Union_Building.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Indoor climbing at the Student Union Building.</div></div></div>
<p>The University of British Columbia has a number of athletic facilities open to both their varsity teams as well as to their students. The stadium with the largest seating capacity at UBC is the Doug Mitchell Thunderbird Sports Centre. The Doug Mitchell Thunderbird Sports Centre is home to the varsity ice hockey teams and was also used as a venue for the <a href="/wiki/2010_Winter_Olympics" title="2010 Winter Olympics">2010 Winter Olympics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> Other facilities at UBC includes <a href="/wiki/Thunderbird_Stadium" title="Thunderbird Stadium">Thunderbird Stadium</a>, home to the university's football and soccer varsity teams, UBC Aquatic Centre, home to the university's swimming teams, the War Memorial Gymnasium, home to the university's basketball and volleyball varsity teams and Thunderbird Park, home to the university's many other outdoor varsity teams.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup>
</p><p>The university has also had a long history of sending a number of students to represent their countries at the Olympics. Since having its first athlete sent to the Olympics in 1928, a total of 231 individuals from UBC have represented their respective countries at the Olympics. The total number of individual medals athletes from UBC had won was 61, with 19 gold, 21 silver and 24 bronze. The majority of these medals won had come from the sport of rowing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Marching_band">Marching band</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Marching band">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>UBC's marching band, the Thunderbird Marching Band, was founded in September 2012 and is entirely student-run. The band performs at various <a href="/wiki/UBC_Thunderbirds" title="UBC Thunderbirds">Thunderbirds</a> football, basketball, rugby, and hockey games, as well as other campus events. It is the only university-level marching band in Western Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fight_song">Fight song</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Fight song">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Notable among a number of songs commonly played and sung at various events such as <a href="/wiki/Graduation" title="Graduation">commencement</a> and <a href="/wiki/Convocation" title="Convocation">convocation</a>, and athletic games are: "Hail, U.B.C" with words and music by Harold King and "High on Olympus" with words by D.C. Morton and music by J.C.F. Haeffner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus_events">Campus events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Campus events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rosegarden_ubc.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2065" data-file-width="2793" height="237" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Rosegarden_ubc.jpg/320px-Rosegarden_ubc.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Rosegarden_ubc.jpg/480px-Rosegarden_ubc.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Rosegarden_ubc.jpg/640px-Rosegarden_ubc.jpg 2x" width="320"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rosegarden_ubc.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>UBC Rose Garden.</div></div></div>
<p>A small number of large-scale, campus-wide events occur annually at UBC which are organized by university institutions, the AMS, and student constituencies of various faculties and departments. Additionally, a number of unofficial traditions exist at UBC: jumping from the Aquatic Centre's 10-metre diving board late at night and repainting the Engineering <a href="/wiki/Cairn" title="Cairn">cairn</a> so as to advertise other clubs.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:University_of_British_Columbia_Engineering_Cairn.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4920" data-file-width="7362" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/University_of_British_Columbia_Engineering_Cairn.jpg/220px-University_of_British_Columbia_Engineering_Cairn.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/University_of_British_Columbia_Engineering_Cairn.jpg/330px-University_of_British_Columbia_Engineering_Cairn.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/University_of_British_Columbia_Engineering_Cairn.jpg/440px-University_of_British_Columbia_Engineering_Cairn.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:University_of_British_Columbia_Engineering_Cairn.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The UBC Engineering Cairn, a chamfered tetrahedral concrete block with a large red "E" on each of its three sides, shown here in its unvandalised state. Painting the cairn is a favourite hobby of student clubs and rival faculties.</div></div></div>
<p>Several group athletic events take place at UBC every year. Storm the Wall is an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intramural" title="Intramural">intramural</a> relay race put on by UBC Recreation in April, culminating in the climbing of a 12-foot (3.7 m) wall.  Day of the Longboat is an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intramural" title="Intramural">intramural</a> event put on at the end of September/early October by UBC Recreation. It is a major voyageur canoe race with teams competing in a 2 km paddle around the waters of Jericho Sailing Centre. The program is operated by over 120 volunteer students and staff who are responsible for operating every aspect of this program. UBC Recreation's student administrators fill various roles including event planning, sport officiating, public relations and building supervision.
</p><p>Faculty constituencies, such as the Arts Undergraduate Society (AUS) and Science Undergraduate Society (SUS), hold events annually. Many of the major constituencies, such as for Arts, Science, and Engineering, hold their own faculty weeks to celebrate their faculties. The events may include keynote speeches, merchandise sales, and dances. Arts County Fair was an annual concert and party on the last day of classes in April, put on by the AUS and occurring at Thunderbird Stadium.  Past headliners have included <a href="/wiki/Sam_Roberts" title="Sam Roberts">Sam Roberts</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_New_Pornographers" title="The New Pornographers">The New Pornographers</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Metric_(band)" title="Metric (band)">Metric</a>.  Due to increasing financial difficulties (mostly resulting from mounting security and related costs) the AUS announced they would not continue the event in 2008. In its place, the Alma Mater Society of UBC hosted the AMS Block Party to celebrate the end of classes.
</p><p>During the Spring exam season, the Ski &amp; Board Club organizes the Undie Run, a charity event that encourages people to donate their clothes to the Big Brothers &amp; Sisters organization in Vancouver.  Students meet at the Student Union Building, remove the clothes they are going to donate, and then run around campus in their underwear. Students run through places like the Irvin K. Barber Centre and Place Vanier Residence before ending at the Martha Piper Plaza fountain.
</p><p>To celebrate the beginning of classes, UBC Orientations organizes several events for first-year students, such as Imagine UBC, GALA, and UBC Jump Start. Imagine UBC is an orientation day and <a href="/wiki/Pep_rally" title="Pep rally">pep rally</a> for first-year undergraduate students that replaces the first day of class after Labour Day at UBC Vancouver.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rape_chant_controversy">Rape chant controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Rape chant controversy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>During the 2013 Imagine day, a post on <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> showed first year students in the Sauder School of Business singing a chant that bragged about rape. The chant, dating back to at least 1993, had already created controversy at <a href="/wiki/Saint_Mary%27s_University_(Halifax)#Rape_chant_controversy" title="Saint Mary's University (Halifax)">Saint Mary's University</a> days earlier.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chant-hp_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-chant-hp-145">[145]</a></sup> The Commerce Undergraduate Society stated that it had been trying to scale back the cheer by using it in buses but not outside. Four CUS leaders resigned over the incident and 81 others were required to perform an unspecified amount of community service by the UBC President, Stephen Toope.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chant-cbc_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-chant-cbc-146">[146]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Model_United_Nations">Model United Nations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Model United Nations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In March 2012, UBC was the partner Host University of the <a href="/wiki/Harvard_World_Model_United_Nations" title="Harvard World Model United Nations">Harvard World Model United Nations</a> Conference (WorldMUN 2012 Vancouver). As the world's largest student-organized Model UN conference, this was also the largest student conference to have ever been organized by UBC and the largest student conference on Canadian soil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> There were 2,200 student delegates and nearly 200 faculty advisors from 270 universities from over 60 countries. The organizing committee amassed over 500 student volunteers from across the UBC campus and the local student community to execute the week-long event.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
